<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>The <b>Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards</b>, also known as the <b>KCAs</b> or <b>Kids Choice Awards</b>, is an annual awards show that airs on the <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable channel</a>, which is usually held on a Saturday night in late March or early April, that honors the year's biggest <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie" title="Movie">movie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> acts, as voted by Nickelodeon viewers. Winners receive a hollow orange <a href="/wiki/Blimp" title="Blimp">blimp</a> figurine, a logo outline for much of the network's 1984–2009 era, which also functions as a <a href="/wiki/Kaleidoscope" title="Kaleidoscope">kaleidoscope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The show features numerous celebrity guests and musical acts. In recent years, slime stunts have been incorporated into the show. The KCAs also host live entertainment. It has also been known to overwhelmingly cover people with the network's trademark <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_slime_(You_Can%27t_Do_That_on_Television)" title="Green slime (You Can't Do That on Television)">green slime</a>. The series <i><a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants" title="SpongeBob SquarePants">SpongeBob SquarePants</a></i> has won the most KCA awards, with twelve overall through the series' run. Individually, <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a> has won the most trophies with ten, followed by <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a> (9), <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Bynes" title="Amanda Bynes">Amanda Bynes</a> (7), <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> (6), <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> (5), <a href="/wiki/Hilary_Duff" title="Hilary Duff">Hilary Duff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a> (4), <a href="/wiki/Ross_Lynch" title="Ross Lynch">Ross Lynch</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/Drake_Bell" title="Drake Bell">Drake Bell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>. <a href="/wiki/Whoopi_Goldberg" title="Whoopi Goldberg">Whoopi Goldberg</a> is the only person to have won a Kids' Choice Award, along with the mainstream "<a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_won_Academy,_Emmy,_Grammy,_and_Tony_Awards" title="List of people who have won Academy, Emmy, Grammy, and Tony Awards">EGOT</a>" combination of an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rosie_O%27Donnell" title="Rosie O'Donnell">Rosie O'Donnell</a> (8) and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Black" title="Jack Black">Jack Black</a> (3) have hosted the show the most times.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alan_Goodman" title="Alan Goodman">Alan Goodman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albie_Hecht" title="Albie Hecht">Albie Hecht</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fred_Seibert" title="Fred Seibert">Fred Seibert</a> created the awards show after Nickelodeon produced a show called <i>The Big Ballot</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> in 1986, named for the ballots kids voted with. To vote, the viewers would send in ballots and then before the show, the ballots would be counted and the winners would tape a thank you video that would be shown during the program. Goodman, Hecht, and Seibert felt that the network needed a bigger, more exciting platform.</p>
<p>Hecht selected the awards logo from a series of network designs created by original logo designers Tom Corey and Scott Nash (<a href="/wiki/Corey_McPherson_Nash" title="Corey McPherson Nash">Corey McPherson Nash</a>, Boston), overseen by Goodman and Seibert (Fred/Alan, Inc., New York).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The award was configured into the current blimp shape/kaleidoscope in 1990. The only change to the award since that time has been to change the embossed logotype on the side of the trophy for 2010 to fit the network's new logo typeface.</p>
<p>As the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> came into widespread use, the voting eventually moved from a combination of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/900_number" title="900 number">900 number</a> telephone voting and ballots either mailed or completed at <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a> locations, to moving exclusively online to the <a href="/wiki/Nick.com" title="Nick.com">network's website</a> and by 2007, <a href="/wiki/Text_messaging" title="Text messaging">text messaging</a>. Early years of Internet voting had the early adoption complications of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballot_stuffing" title="Ballot stuffing">ballot stuffing</a> and even adults voting before a new system where only one vote per Nick.com account became the procedure for voting on the awards (although it is probable adults still cast votes via the texting option, which is connected to a phone number only rather than a screenname, or by creating an account with a false age or having their children vote for a chosen subject instead). In 2010, an <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ITunes_App_Store" title="ITunes App Store">application</a> and mobile browser voting was also added.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2009 KCAs featured a new award called "The Big Green Help Award" which goes to the celebrity who goes above and beyond to help the Earth. The inaugural award was presented to <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>. For the 2010 awards, the "The Big Green Help" award was renamed "The Big Help" award, with <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady</a> <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle Obama</a> winning the first award under the rename.</p>
<p>Unlike traditional awards shows, the Kids' Choice Awards uses other items to announce an award winner rather than a traditional <a href="/wiki/Envelope" title="Envelope">envelope</a>. The show sometimes uses balloons, T-shirts, models, giant letters, stickers (1999, where Amanda put a "Kick Me!" sticky on the model's back and somebody else put a <a href="/wiki/The_Rugrats_Movie" title="The Rugrats Movie">sticker showing the winner's name</a>). and even a foot (2008).</p>
<p>Voting for Canadians became available for the 2010 ceremony with the inauguration of Nickelodeon's <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_(Canada)" title="Nickelodeon (Canada)">Canadian service</a> in November 2009.</p>
<p>In June 2010, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Latin_America" title="Nickelodeon Latin America">Nickelodeon Latin America</a> announced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Awards_Mexico" title="Kids' Choice Awards Mexico">Kids' Choice Awards for Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Other countries with their own Kids' Choice Awards include <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, which are either fully original local productions, or inserted as <a href="/wiki/Continuity_(broadcasting)" title="Continuity (broadcasting)">continuity</a> during their broadcast of the American ceremony.</p>
<p>In August 2011, Nickelodeon Latin America announced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Awards_Argentina" title="Kids' Choice Awards Argentina">Kids' Choice Awards for Argentina</a>.</p>
<p>In June 2014, Nickelodeon Latin America announced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Awards_Colombia" title="Kids' Choice Awards Colombia">Kids' Choice Awards for Colombia</a>.</p>
<p>In July 2014, Nickelodeon presented the <a href="/wiki/2014_Kids%27_Choice_Sports_Awards" title="2014 Kids' Choice Sports Awards">Kids' Choice Sports</a> awards, honoring kids' favorite athletes, teams and sports moments from the year. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Strahan" title="Michael Strahan">Michael Strahan</a> produced and hosted the ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg/250px-2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg/375px-2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg/500px-2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009_KCA_Orange_Carpet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Finishing up with the "Orange Carpet" for the Kids' Choice Awards outside of <a href="/wiki/Pauley_Pavilion" title="Pauley Pavilion">Pauley Pavilion</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA">UCLA</a> campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Kids' Choice Awards are typically held in and around <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. They have been held at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barker_Hangar" title="Barker Hangar">Barker Hangar</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica, California</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl" title="Hollywood Bowl">Hollywood Bowl</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Olympic_Auditorium" title="Grand Olympic Auditorium">Grand Olympic Auditorium</a> in Los Angeles, and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Universal_City,_California" title="Universal City, California">Universal City, California</a>, but mostly at <a href="/wiki/Pauley_Pavilion" title="Pauley Pavilion">Pauley Pavilion</a> on the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">UCLA</a> campus. After renovations to Pauley beginning in 2011, the show was moved to the <a href="/wiki/Galen_Center" title="Galen Center">Galen Center</a> at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> it was expected to be a temporary home, but the network retained Galen for the 2014 ceremony due to the construction of the Meyer and Renee Luskin Conference and Guest Center, making it difficult to have the "Orange Carpet"; the smaller <a href="/wiki/2014_Kids%27_Choice_Sports_Awards" title="2014 Kids' Choice Sports Awards">Kids' Choice Sports</a> awards had its first ceremony in 2014 at Pauley. For the 2015 and 2016 shows, the ceremony occurred at the remodeled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood)" title="The Forum (Inglewood)">Forum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood, California</a> and moved back at the Galen Center for 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceremony_hosts">Ceremony hosts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ceremony hosts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 1987 <i>Big Ballot</i> studio show was unhosted.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hosts_for_multiple_years">Hosts for multiple years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hosts for multiple years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jack_Black" title="Jack Black">Jack Black</a> hosted in 2006, 2008, and the 2011 shows and so far the first host after <a href="/wiki/Rosie_O%27Donnell" title="Rosie O'Donnell">Rosie O'Donnell</a> to host the show at least twice. <a href="/wiki/Candace_Cameron_Bure" title="Candace Cameron Bure">Candace Cameron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a> were the first hosts before O'Donnell to host at least twice (Cameron 1990 and 1994, Houston 1995 and 1996).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_colored_awards">Special colored awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Special colored awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>These blimps are not orange like the regular blimps and the winners are chosen by the Nickelodeon staff, not the viewers. There is the gold Hall of Fame Award (1991–2000), the silver Wannabe Award (2001–2008), the green Big Green Help Award (2009), the silver glitter Big Help Award (2010–2012), and the Lifetime Achievement Award (2014–present)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Hall_of_Fame_Award">The Hall of Fame Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Hall of Fame Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Hall of Fame Award</b> (a gold version of the Blimp award) was presented to those whose accomplishments, fame and popularity set them above everyone else. Initially, the award was chosen by the kids from a slate of nominees. Actors, athletes and singers were all eligible for the award, with ballots containing nominees from multiple categories.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Wannabe_Award">The Wannabe Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Wannabe Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Wannabe Award</b> (a silver version of the Blimp award) is presented to the best celebrity <a href="/wiki/Role_model" title="Role model">role model</a> or inspiration (or the person whom the kids <i><b>want to be</b></i> like). The winner is determined prior to the awards without voter input. As of 2009, the only person to have won the Wannabe award and the Hall of Fame award is <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a>. These awards replaced the Hall of Fame awards following the show in 2000.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Big_Help_Award">The Big Help Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Big Help Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Big Green Help (The Big Help) Award</b> (originally a green-colored trophy, silver in 2012) is presented to a person who goes above and beyond to help the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifetime_Achievement_Award">Lifetime Achievement Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Lifetime Achievement Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Nickelodeon Lifetime Achievement Award</b> is presented to a network employee on or off camera that has contributed heavily to the network's success and entertained children with their work.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Final_Slime_a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Final_Slime_a.jpg/250px-Final_Slime_a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Final_Slime_a.jpg/375px-Final_Slime_a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Final_Slime_a.jpg/500px-Final_Slime_a.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Final_Slime_a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The final slime at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2010 Kids' Choice Awards">2010 Kids' Choice Awards</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During a ceremony, sometimes a celebrity might not know when they are going to be slimed onstage or offstage, though it is meant as an honor, rather than the comedic humiliation of where the concept originated, with the early Nickelodeon series <i><a href="/wiki/You_Can%27t_Do_That_on_Television#Slime" title="You Can't Do That on Television">You Can't Do That on Television</a></i>. Hosts have also been slimed, mostly in the finale of the show. Below is a list of all the celebrities that have been slimed over the past years at the Kids' Choice Awards. No celebrity sliming took place in 1992 as the entire audience was slimed instead.</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Slime_stunts">Slime stunts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Slime stunts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Started in 2002, the show began its annual <i><b>World Record Slime Stunts</b></i>. Olympians, extreme sports stars and daredevils participate in special stunts performed live on national television—often involving landing into the trademark green slime.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Celebrity (ies)</th>
<th width="85%">Stunt synopsis</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2002</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Dave_Mirra" title="Dave Mirra">Dave Mirra</a></td>
<td>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_Motocross" title="Bicycle Motocross">BMX</a> pro-biker broke his own record for a double back flip on a BMX bike and landed in a 5,000 gallon tank of green slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2003</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Tony_Hawk" title="Tony Hawk">Tony Hawk</a></td>
<td>The <a href="/wiki/Skateboard" title="Skateboard">skateboarding</a> champion skateboarded into an 11,000 gallon tank of green slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2004</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Mat_Hoffman" title="Mat Hoffman">Mat Hoffman</a></td>
<td>The BMX pro performed the "World Record Skydiving Bike Jump" landing in a lakefull of green slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2005</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a></td>
<td>The billionaire at the time enjoying a resurgence of popularity with his TV series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Apprentice_(US_TV_series)" title="The Apprentice (US TV series)">The Apprentice</a></i> "fired" a human cannonball into the air, landing in a net laced with green slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2006</td>
<td>Ryan St. Onge</td>
<td>In a live remote from the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Olympic_Park" title="Utah Olympic Park">Utah Olympic Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Park_City,_Utah" title="Park City, Utah">Park City, Utah</a>, the U.S. Olympic Freestyle Aerial <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">Skier</a> skied into 10,000 gallons of green slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2007</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ron_Jones_(athlete)" title="Ron Jones (athlete)">Ron Jones</a></td>
<td>Bungee jumping into a pool of slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" rowspan="4">2008</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Jack_Black" title="Jack Black">Jack Black</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a></td>
<td><i>Kids Choice 2008</i> had many slime stunts all hosted by professional boxer <a href="/wiki/Laila_Ali" title="Laila Ali">Laila Ali</a>. Depending on the outcome of the stunt, a certain amount of green slime was added to a slime vat backstage which was called throughout as the "Slime Meter". The slime was used later on at the end of the show, in supposedly the "World's Longest Celebrity Sliming," in which <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a> joined host <a href="/wiki/Jack_Black" title="Jack Black">Jack Black</a> to be slimed for one solid minute. Host Black even remarked about how 27 tons of slime (the grand total) could fit in a vat that only held 25 tons.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a></td>
<td>In the first stunt, affectionately called the "Slime-o-Lition Derby", the pop star had 45 seconds to ride the Kids' Choice Bobble Head Kart. The choices were the shark-themed "<a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)">Jaws</a> Jalopy", a <a href="/wiki/Hot_dog" title="Hot dog">hot dog</a>-shaped "Weiner Wagon" and the winner, the Jack Black Bobble Head Kart which was essentially a go-kart with a giant Jack Black head on the top. Akon successfully completed the course adding 10 tons of slime to the vat, "plus 5 for finishing" bringing the total to 15 tons.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a></td>
<td>The famous R&amp;B singer performed the second stunt manning a "slime hose," firing at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumo_wrestling" title="Sumo wrestling">sumo wrestler</a> and propelling him in costume along a long platform. The amount of slime added to the vat was determined by how far the "human target" was propelled by the spray of slime. Viewers voting online picked the sumo wrestler over his competitor, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scuba_diver" title="Scuba diver">Scuba diver</a>. The "human target" was launched all the way to the 5-ton mark bringing the total of slime in the vat to 20 tons.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Heidi_Klum" title="Heidi Klum">Heidi Klum</a></td>
<td>The last stunt was performed by the supermodel or as host Black called her "Heidi the Human Dart". Klum was attached by a harness to a long cable, allowing her to swing freely in which she did. Armed with a pad of spikes, she swung between her platform and what was a trampoline-like wall covered in slime balloons. For every slime balloon Klum popped in 30 seconds, one more ton of slime was added to the vat. Kids voted online to determine exactly what type of spike pad Klum would use to pop the balloons. The choices were the hand-worn "mittens" and the winner the "butt pad" which unanimously beat out the mittens. Klum popped 7 balloons on the wall, adding 7 more tons of slime to the vat and bringing the total of slime in the vat to 27 tons.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2009</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Will_Ferrell" title="Will Ferrell">Will Ferrell</a></td>
<td>The comedian-actor slid down a slime-covered slide that was placed on top of Janss Steps on the UCLA campus, on a luge head first into a pool of slime.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" rowspan="2">2010</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apolo_Anton_Ohno" title="Apolo Anton Ohno">Apolo Anton Ohno</a></td>
<td>Two stunts were featured at the 2010 awards. First, eight-time <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">Olympic</a> medalist Ohno was catapulted into slime by sling shot with the help of <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a> wrestler <a href="/wiki/John_Cena" title="John Cena">John Cena</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Trainor" title="Jerry Trainor">Jerry Trainor</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Jackson_Rathbone" title="Jackson Rathbone">Jackson Rathbone</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Nicola_Peltz" title="Nicola Peltz">Nicola Peltz</a></td>
<td>For the second stunt, to promote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Airbender" title="The Last Airbender">The Last Airbender</a></i> stars Peltz and Rathbone along with <i><a href="/wiki/ICarly" title="ICarly">iCarly</a></i> star Trainor were featured in a bending-slime event. Since Peltz's character is a "water-bender", she bent the slime towards Trainor and Rathbone.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2011</td>
<td>Kelvin Ramer</td>
<td>Ramer's monster truck, rebodied and relivered for the event, jumps over a 50-foot Nickelodeon blimp award into a pool of slime. It was hosted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Show_(wrestler)" title="Big Show (wrestler)">Paul "The Big Show" Wight</a> who said that it was the most dangerous Kids' Choice slime stunt ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2012</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Big_Show" title="Big Show">Big Show</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a></td>
<td>A slime themed wrestling match between <a href="/wiki/Big_Show" title="Big Show">Big Show</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a>. When either The Big Show or The Miz hits the special cannons on each corner of the ring, slime shoots out and covers the audience. The Big Show defeated The Miz when he threw him over the ring and into a pool of slime. Afterwards, The Big Show was slimed for his ultimate reward.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2014</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Dave_England" title="Dave England">Dave England</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jukka_Hilden" title="Jukka Hilden">Jukka Hilden</a></td>
<td>Kids got pick between 3 slime stunts and the one of the highest amount of votes would win. It was between Ultimate Slime Rodeo, High Speed Bathtub Race or a Slippery Obstacle Course, eventually the slime rodeo won. Both Dave and Jukka rode on Horses that were slime hoses and whoever held on the longest would win. Dave eventually held on the longest and won.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2015</td>
<td>Cast of <a href="/wiki/The_Thundermans" title="The Thundermans">The Thundermans</a></td>
<td>Slime Car Wash</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">2016</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bethany_Mota" title="Bethany Mota">Bethany Mota</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Dallas" title="Cameron Dallas">Cameron Dallas</a></td>
<td>Slime Soakers</td>
</tr>
</table>

<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
